<td><a href="/wiki/.ao" title=".ao">.ao</a></td>

</table>
<p><b>Angola</b> <span class="nowrap"><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/æ/ short 'a' in 'bad'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">æ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'n' in 'nigh'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">n</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ˈ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'g' in 'guy'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ɡ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/oʊ/ long 'o' in 'bode'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">oʊ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'l' in 'lie'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">l</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ə</span></a></span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span></span>, officially the <b>Republic of Angola</b> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt"><i>República de Angola</i></span> <small>pronounced:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Portuguese_and_Galician" title="Help:IPA for Portuguese and Galician">[ʁɛˈpublikɐ dɨ ɐ̃ˈɡɔlɐ]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Kikongo" title="Kikongo" class="mw-redirect">Kikongo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kimbundu" title="Kimbundu">Kimbundu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Umbundu" title="Umbundu">Umbundu</a>: <i>Repubilika ya Ngola</i>), is a country in Southern Africa. It is the seventh largest country in Africa, and is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a> on the south, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> on the north, and <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> on the east; its west coast is on the Atlantic Ocean and <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a> is its capital city. The <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">exclave</a> province of <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_Province" title="Cabinda Province">Cabinda</a> has borders with the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>.</p>
<p>The Portuguese were present in some – mostly coastal – points of the territory of what is now Angola from the 16th century, interacting in diverse ways with the peoples who lived there. In the 19th century, settlers slowly and hesitantly began to establish themselves in the interior. Angola as a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_West_Africa" title="Portuguese West Africa" class="mw-redirect">Portuguese colony</a> encompassing the present territory was not established until the early 20th century, after the <a href="/wiki/Mbunda_people" title="Mbunda people">Mbunda</a> resistance and abduction of their King, <a href="/wiki/Mwene_Mbandu_Kapova_I_of_Mbunda" title="Mwene Mbandu Kapova I of Mbunda">Mwene Mbandu I Lyondthzi Kapova</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SeeRene_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SeeRene-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Independence was achieved in 1975, after a <a href="/wiki/Angolan_War_of_Independence" title="Angolan War of Independence">protracted liberation war</a>. After independence, Angola descended into an intense <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">civil war from 1975 to 2002</a>. Despite the civil war, areas such as <a href="/wiki/Baixa_de_Cassanje" title="Baixa de Cassanje">Baixa de Cassanje</a> continue a lineage of kings which have included the former King <a href="/wiki/Kambamba_Kulaxingo" title="Kambamba Kulaxingo">Kambamba Kulaxingo</a> and current King Dianhenga Aspirante Mjinji Kulaxingo.</p>
<p>Angola has vast mineral and petroleum reserves, and its economy has on average grown at a double-digit pace since the 1990s, especially following the end of the civil war. In spite of this, standards of living remain low for the majority of the population, and <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality rates</a> in Angola are among the worst in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Angola is considered to be economically disparate, with the majority of the nation's <a href="/wiki/Wealth_concentration" title="Wealth concentration">wealth concentrated</a> in a disproportionately small sector of the population.</p>
<p>Angola is a member state of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Union" title="Latin Union">Latin Union</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The name <i>Angola</i> comes from the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> colonial name <i><a href="/wiki/Angola_(Portugal)" title="Angola (Portugal)" class="mw-redirect">Reino de Angola</a> (Kingdom of Angola)</i>, appearing as early as <a href="/wiki/Dias_de_Novais" title="Dias de Novais" class="mw-redirect">Dias de Novais</a>'s 1571 charter.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Toponym" title="Toponym" class="mw-redirect">toponym</a> was derived by the Portuguese from the title <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_Ngolas_of_Ndongo" title="List of Ngolas of Ndongo">ngola</a></i> held by the kings of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ndongo" title="Kingdom of Ndongo">Ndongo</a>. Ndongo was a kingdom in the highlands, between the <a href="/wiki/Kwanza_River" title="Kwanza River" class="mw-redirect">Kwanza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lukala_River" title="Lukala River" class="mw-redirect">Lukala Rivers</a>, nominally tributary to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">king of Kongo</a> but which was seeking greater independence during the 16th century.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Angola" title="History of Angola">History of Angola</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_migrations_and_political_units">Early migrations and political units</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early migrations and political units">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KingdomNdongo1711.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/KingdomNdongo1711.png/220px-KingdomNdongo1711.png" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/KingdomNdongo1711.png/330px-KingdomNdongo1711.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/KingdomNdongo1711.png/440px-KingdomNdongo1711.png 2x" data-file-width="774" data-file-height="540" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KingdomNdongo1711.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Territory comprising <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ndongo" title="Kingdom of Ndongo">Kingdom of Ndongo</a>, present-day Angola</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Khoisan" title="Khoisan">Khoisan</a> <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherers</a> are the earliest known modern human inhabitants of the area. They were largely absorbed or replaced by <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu peoples</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_expansion" title="Bantu expansion">Bantu migrations</a>, though small numbers remain in parts of southern Angola to the present day. The Bantu came from the north, probably from somewhere near the present-day Republic of <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (March 2015)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup> The establishment of the Bantu took many centuries and gave rise to various groups who took on different ethnic characteristics.</p>
<p>During this time, the Bantu established a number of political units ("kingdoms", "empires") in most parts of what today is Angola. The best known of these is the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Kongo" title="Kingdom of the Kongo" class="mw-redirect">Kingdom of the Kongo</a> that had its centre in the northwest of contemporary Angola, but included important regions in the west of present day <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Congo" title="Republic of Congo" class="mw-redirect">Republic of Congo</a>, and in southern <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>. It established trade routes with other trading cities and civilizations up and down the coast of southwestern and West Africa and even with the <a href="/wiki/Great_Zimbabwe" title="Great Zimbabwe">Great Zimbabwe</a> <a href="/wiki/Mutapa_Empire" title="Mutapa Empire" class="mw-redirect">Mutapa Empire</a>, but engaged in little or no transoceanic trade.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Story_of_Africa_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Story_of_Africa-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Others include the <a href="/wiki/Mbunda_people" title="Mbunda people">Mbunda</a>, whose <a href="/wiki/Mbunda_Kingdom" title="Mbunda Kingdom">Kingdom</a> was established in the fifteenth century<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> at the confluence of Kwilu and Kasai rivers, in the south of present day Democratic Republic of the Congo, after a misunderstanding in Kola, also known as the origin of the Lunda and the Luba Kingdoms. The Mbunda trace their origin from <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> trekking southwards through Kola where they came in contact with the Luba and Ruund people. They reached what is now Angola in the sixteenth century, where they encountered the Khoisan, Bushmen and other groups considerably less technologically advanced, whom they easily dominated with their superior knowledge of metal-working, ceramics and agriculture. <a href="/wiki/Mbunda_Kingdom" title="Mbunda Kingdom">The Mbunda Kingdom</a> in Mbundaland, southeast of the now Angola endured until late nineteenth century, one of the oldest and biggest ethnic grouping in Southern Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-RobertPapstein_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RobertPapstein-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_colonization">Portuguese colonization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Portuguese colonization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Colonial_history_of_Angola" title="Colonial history of Angola">Colonial history of Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Angola_(Portugal)" title="Angola (Portugal)" class="mw-redirect">Angola (Portugal)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Queen_Nzinga_1657.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Queen_Nzinga_1657.png/220px-Queen_Nzinga_1657.png" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Queen_Nzinga_1657.png/330px-Queen_Nzinga_1657.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Queen_Nzinga_1657.png/440px-Queen_Nzinga_1657.png 2x" data-file-width="1438" data-file-height="953" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Queen_Nzinga_1657.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Queen_Nzinga" title="Queen Nzinga" class="mw-redirect">Queen Nzinga</a> in peace negotiations with the Portuguese governor in <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a>, 1657.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kongo_audience.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Kongo_audience.jpg/220px-Kongo_audience.jpg" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Kongo_audience.jpg/330px-Kongo_audience.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Kongo_audience.jpg/440px-Kongo_audience.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="491" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kongo_audience.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An image depicting Portuguese encounter with Kongo Royal family</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The geographical areas now designated as Angola entered into contact with the Portuguese in the late 15th century, concretely in 1483, when Portugal established relations with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kongo</a> State, which stretched from modern <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a> in the north to the <a href="/wiki/Kwanza_River" title="Kwanza River" class="mw-redirect">Kwanza River</a> in the south. In this context, the Portuguese established a small trade-post at the port of Mpinda, in <a href="/wiki/Soyo" title="Soyo">Soyo</a>. The Portuguese explorer <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Dias_de_Novais" title="Paulo Dias de Novais">Paulo Dias de Novais</a> founded <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a> in 1575 as "São Paulo de Loanda", with a hundred families of settlers and four hundred soldiers. <a href="/wiki/Benguela" title="Benguela">Benguela</a>, a Portuguese fort from 1587 which became a town in 1617, was another important early settlement they founded and ruled. The Portuguese would establish several settlements, forts and trading posts along the coastal strip of current-day Angola, which relied on the <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Angola" title="Slavery in Angola">slave trade</a>, commerce in raw materials, and the exchange of goods for survival.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a> provided a large number of black slaves to merchants and to slave dealers in Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-Fleisch_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fleisch-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> European traders would export manufactured goods to the coast of Africa where they would be exchanged for slaves. Within the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a>, most black African slaves were traded to Portuguese merchants who bought them to sell as cheap labour for use on Brazilian agricultural plantations. This trade would last until the first half of the 19th century. According to <a href="/wiki/John_Iliffe_(historian)" title="John Iliffe (historian)">John Iliffe</a>, "Portuguese records of Angola from the 16th century show that a great <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famine</a> occurred on average every seventy years; accompanied by epidemic disease, it might kill one-third or one-half of the population, destroying the demographic growth of a generation and forcing colonists back into the river valleys".<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Portuguese gradually took control of the coastal strip during the 16th century by a series of treaties and wars, forming the Portuguese colony of Angola. Taking advantage of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Restoration_War" title="Portuguese Restoration War">Portuguese Restoration War</a>, the Dutch occupied <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a> from 1641 to 1648, where they allied with local peoples, consolidating their colonial rule against the remaining Portuguese resistance. In 1648, a fleet under the command of <a href="/wiki/Salvador_de_S%C3%A1" title="Salvador de Sá">Salvador de Sá</a> retook Luanda for Portugal and initiated a conquest of the lost territories, which restored Portugal to its former possessions by 1650. Treaties regulated relations with <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kongo</a> in 1649 and Njinga's Kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Matamba" title="Matamba" class="mw-redirect">Matamba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ndongo" title="Ndongo" class="mw-redirect">Ndongo</a> in 1656. The conquest of <a href="/wiki/Pungo_Andongo" title="Pungo Andongo" class="mw-redirect">Pungo Andongo</a> in 1671 was the last major Portuguese expansion from Luanda outwards, as attempts to invade Kongo in 1670 and Matamba in 1681 failed. Portugal also expanded its territory behind the colony of Benguela to some extent, but until the 19th century the inroads from Luanda and Benguela were very limited, and Portugal had neither the intention nor the means to carry out a large scale territorial occupation and colonization.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:King_Mwene_Mbandu_Lyondthzi_Kapova_I.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/King_Mwene_Mbandu_Lyondthzi_Kapova_I.jpg/220px-King_Mwene_Mbandu_Lyondthzi_Kapova_I.jpg" width="220" height="289" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/King_Mwene_Mbandu_Lyondthzi_Kapova_I.jpg/330px-King_Mwene_Mbandu_Lyondthzi_Kapova_I.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/King_Mwene_Mbandu_Lyondthzi_Kapova_I.jpg/440px-King_Mwene_Mbandu_Lyondthzi_Kapova_I.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1618" data-file-height="2124" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:King_Mwene_Mbandu_Lyondthzi_Kapova_I.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Mwene_Mbandu_Kapova_I_of_Mbunda" title="Mwene Mbandu Kapova I of Mbunda">King Mwene Mbandu I Lyondthzi Kapova</a>, the 21st <a href="/wiki/Mbunda_Kingdom" title="Mbunda Kingdom">Monarch of the Mbunda Kingdom</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Embarque_tropas_para_angola_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Embarque_tropas_para_angola_1.jpg/220px-Embarque_tropas_para_angola_1.jpg" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Embarque_tropas_para_angola_1.jpg/330px-Embarque_tropas_para_angola_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Embarque_tropas_para_angola_1.jpg/440px-Embarque_tropas_para_angola_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2178" data-file-height="1471" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Embarque_tropas_para_angola_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Portuguese troops heading for Angola during <a href="/wiki/German_campaign_in_Angola" title="German campaign in Angola">World War I</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The process resulted in few gains until the 1880s. Development of the hinterland began after the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Conference" title="Berlin Conference">Berlin Conference</a> in 1885 fixed the colony's borders, and British and Portuguese investment fostered mining, railways, and agriculture based on various forced-labour systems. Full Portuguese administrative control of the hinterland did not establish itself until the beginning of the 20th century, after the <a href="/wiki/Mbunda_people" title="Mbunda people">Mbunda</a> resistance and abduction of their King, <a href="/wiki/Mwene_Mbandu_Kapova_I_of_Mbunda" title="Mwene Mbandu Kapova I of Mbunda">Mwene Mbandu I Lyondthzi Kapova</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-SeeRene_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SeeRene-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> eventually dislodged the <a href="/wiki/Mbunda_Kingdom" title="Mbunda Kingdom">Mbunda Kingdom</a> extending Angolan territory over Mbundaland.<sup id="cite_ref-RobertPapstein_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RobertPapstein-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1951 the Portuguese government designated the colony as an overseas province of Portugal, called the <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Province_of_Angola" title="Overseas Province of Angola" class="mw-redirect">Overseas Province of Angola</a>.</p>
<p>Portugal had a minimalist presence in Angola for nearly five hundred years, and early calls for independence provoked little reaction amongst the population. More overtly political organisations first appeared in the 1950s and began to make organised demands for <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">self-determination</a>, especially in international forums such as the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Portugal)" title="Estado Novo (Portugal)">Portuguese regime</a>, meanwhile, refused to accede to the demands for independence, provoking an armed conflict that started in 1961 when black guerrillas attacked both white and black civilians in cross-border operations in northeastern Angola. The war came to be known as the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Colonial_War" title="Portuguese Colonial War">Colonial War</a>. In this struggle, the principal protagonists included, the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Movement_for_the_Liberation_of_Angola" title="People's Movement for the Liberation of Angola" class="mw-redirect">People's Movement for the Liberation of Angola</a> (MPLA), founded in 1956, the <a href="/wiki/National_Front_for_the_Liberation_of_Angola" title="National Front for the Liberation of Angola" class="mw-redirect">National Front for the Liberation of Angola</a> (FNLA), which appeared in 1961 and the <a href="/wiki/National_Union_for_the_Total_Independence_of_Angola" title="National Union for the Total Independence of Angola" class="mw-redirect">National Union for the Total Independence of Angola</a> (UNITA), founded in 1966.</p>
<p>After many years of conflict that led to the weakening of all the insurgent parties, Angola gained its independence on 11 November 1975, after the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">1974 coup d'état</a> in Lisbon, Portugal, which overthrew the Portuguese regime headed by <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_Caetano" title="Marcelo Caetano">Marcelo Caetano</a>.</p>
<p>Portugal's <a href="/wiki/Movimento_das_For%C3%A7as_Armadas" title="Movimento das Forças Armadas" class="mw-redirect">new revolutionary leaders</a> began in 1974 a process of political change at home and accepted independence for its former colonies abroad. In Angola a fight for dominance broke out immediately between the three nationalist movements. The events prompted a mass exodus of Portuguese citizens, creating up to 300 000 destitute Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugees</a>—the <i><a href="/wiki/White_African#Portuguese_in_Africa" title="White African" class="mw-redirect">retornados</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> The new Portuguese government tried to mediate an understanding between the three competing movements, and succeeded in getting them to agree, on paper, to form a common government. But in the end none of the African parties respected the commitments made, and military force resolved the issue.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_civil_war">Independence and civil war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Independence and civil war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:View_over_Lunda_3.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/View_over_Lunda_3.JPG/220px-View_over_Lunda_3.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/View_over_Lunda_3.JPG/330px-View_over_Lunda_3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/View_over_Lunda_3.JPG/440px-View_over_Lunda_3.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:View_over_Lunda_3.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Monument to the memory of <a href="/wiki/Agostinho_Neto" title="Agostinho Neto">Agostinho Neto</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_War_of_Independence" title="Angolan War of Independence">Angolan struggle for independence</a>, in Luanda</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Angolan_War_of_Independence" title="Angolan War of Independence">Angolan War of Independence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">Angolan Civil War</a></div>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/1980s_in_Angola" title="1980s in Angola">1980s in Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/1990s_in_Angola" title="1990s in Angola">1990s in Angola</a></div>
<p>After it gained independence in November 1975, Angola experienced a devastating <a href="/wiki/Civil_war" title="Civil war">civil war</a> which lasted several decades, claimed millions of lives and produced many refugees.<sup id="cite_ref-Norrie_MacQueen_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Norrie_MacQueen-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Following <a href="/wiki/Alvor_Agreement" title="Alvor Agreement">negotiations held in Portugal</a>, itself experiencing severe social and political turmoil and uncertainty due to the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">April 1974 revolution</a>, Angola's three main guerrilla groups agreed to establish a transitional government in January 1975.</p>
<p>Within two months, however, the FNLA, MPLA and UNITA had started fighting each other and the country began splitting into zones controlled by rival armed political groups. The superpowers quickly became involved in the conflict, which became a flash point for the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. The United States, <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a> (today's <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>) and South Africa supported the FNLA and UNITA.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> supported the MPLA.</p>
<p>In the beginning of the Angolan Civil War, most of the half-million Portuguese who lived in Angola – and who had accounted for the majority of the skilled work in the public administration, agriculture, industries and trade – fled the country, leaving its once prosperous and growing economy in a state of <a href="/wiki/Bankruptcy" title="Bankruptcy">bankruptcy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During most of this period, 1975–1990, the MPLA organised and maintained a socialist régime.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ceasefire_with_UNITA">Ceasefire with UNITA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Ceasefire with UNITA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cabinda,_R._Congo,_D.R._Congo,_Angola.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Cabinda%2C_R._Congo%2C_D.R._Congo%2C_Angola.png/220px-Cabinda%2C_R._Congo%2C_D.R._Congo%2C_Angola.png" width="220" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Cabinda%2C_R._Congo%2C_D.R._Congo%2C_Angola.png/330px-Cabinda%2C_R._Congo%2C_D.R._Congo%2C_Angola.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/70/Cabinda%2C_R._Congo%2C_D.R._Congo%2C_Angola.png 2x" data-file-width="380" data-file-height="370" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cabinda,_R._Congo,_D.R._Congo,_Angola.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Cabinda_Province" title="Cabinda Province">Cabinda Province</a></div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00ff00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Republic of the Congo</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0000ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Democratic Republic of the Congo</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff00ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;The rest of Angola</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2000s_in_Angola" title="2000s in Angola">2000s in Angola</a></div>
<p>On 22 March 2002, <a href="/wiki/Jonas_Savimbi" title="Jonas Savimbi">Jonas Savimbi</a>, the leader of UNITA, was killed in combat with government troops. A cease-fire was reached by the two factions shortly afterwards.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> UNITA gave up its armed wing and assumed the role of major opposition party, although in the knowledge that in the present regime a legitimate democratic election was impossible. Although the political situation of the country began to stabilize, regular democratic processes were not established before the <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Angola" title="Elections in Angola">Elections in Angola</a> in 2008 and 2012 and the adoption of a new <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Angola" title="Constitution of Angola">Constitution of Angola</a> in 2010, all of which strengthened the prevailing <a href="/wiki/Dominant-party_system" title="Dominant-party system">Dominant-party system</a>. MPLA head officials continue e.g. to be given senior positions in top level companies or other fields, although a few outstanding UNITA figures are given some shares in the economic as well as in the military share.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Among Angola's major problems are a serious humanitarian crisis (a result of the prolonged war), the abundance of <a href="/wiki/Minefield" title="Minefield" class="mw-redirect">minefields</a>, the continuation of the political, and to a much lesser degree, military activities in favour of the independence of the northern <a href="/wiki/Exclave" title="Exclave" class="mw-redirect">exclave</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_(province)" title="Cabinda (province)" class="mw-redirect">Cabinda</a>, carried out in the context of the protracted <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_Conflict" title="Cabinda Conflict" class="mw-redirect">Cabinda Conflict</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Frente_para_a_Liberta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_do_Enclave_de_Cabinda" title="Frente para a Libertação do Enclave de Cabinda" class="mw-redirect">Frente para a Libertação do Enclave de Cabinda</a>, but most of all, the dilapidation of the country's rich mineral resources by the regime. While most of the internally displaced have now settled around the capital, in the so-called "Musseques", the general situation for Angolans remains desperate.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beach_of_Coatinha_in_Benguela,_Angola.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Beach_of_Coatinha_in_Benguela%2C_Angola.jpg/220px-Beach_of_Coatinha_in_Benguela%2C_Angola.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Beach_of_Coatinha_in_Benguela%2C_Angola.jpg/330px-Beach_of_Coatinha_in_Benguela%2C_Angola.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Beach_of_Coatinha_in_Benguela%2C_Angola.jpg/440px-Beach_of_Coatinha_in_Benguela%2C_Angola.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>

</div>

<div class="thumb tright">

Topographic map of Angola.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Angola" title="Geography of Angola">Geography of Angola</a></div>
<p>At 1,246,620&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (481,321&#160;sq&#160;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Angola is the world's twenty-third largest country. It is comparable in size to <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a>, or twice the size of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> or <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>. It lies mostly between latitudes <a href="/wiki/4th_parallel_south" title="4th parallel south">4°</a> and <a href="/wiki/18th_parallel_south" title="18th parallel south">18°S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/12th_meridian_east" title="12th meridian east">12°</a> and <a href="/wiki/24th_meridian_east" title="24th meridian east">24°E</a>.</p>
<p>Angola is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> to the east, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> to the north-east, and the <a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_Ocean" title="South Atlantic Ocean" class="mw-redirect">South Atlantic Ocean</a> to the west. The coastal <a href="/wiki/Exclave" title="Exclave" class="mw-redirect">exclave</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_(province)" title="Cabinda (province)" class="mw-redirect">Cabinda</a> in the north, borders the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> to the north, and the Democratic Republic of the Congo to the south.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> Angola's capital, <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a>, lies on the Atlantic coast in the northwest of the country.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Angola" title="Climate of Angola" class="mw-redirect">Climate of Angola</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_02.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_02.JPG/220px-Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_02.JPG" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_02.JPG/330px-Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_02.JPG/440px-Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_02.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="2432" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_02.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Promenade on <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a> Bay</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Angola has three seasons, a dry season which lasts from May to October, a transitional season with some rain from November to January and a hot, rainy season from February to April. April is the wettest month.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Angola's average temperature on the coast is 16&#160;°C (60&#160;°F) in the winter and 21&#160;°C (70&#160;°F) in the summer, while the interior is generally hotter and dryer.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Angola" title="Politics of Angola">Politics of Angola</a></div>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Angola" title="Elections in Angola">Elections in Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Angola" title="Constitution of Angola">Constitution of Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Angola" title="List of political parties in Angola">List of political parties in Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Angola" title="Foreign relations of Angola">Foreign relations of Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_Angola" title="List of diplomatic missions of Angola">List of diplomatic missions of Angola</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_with_Jose_Eduardo_dos_Santos-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Vladimir_Putin_with_Jose_Eduardo_dos_Santos-1.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_with_Jose_Eduardo_dos_Santos-1.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Vladimir_Putin_with_Jose_Eduardo_dos_Santos-1.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_with_Jose_Eduardo_dos_Santos-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Vladimir_Putin_with_Jose_Eduardo_dos_Santos-1.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_with_Jose_Eduardo_dos_Santos-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="334" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_with_Jose_Eduardo_dos_Santos-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_dos_Santos" title="José Eduardo dos Santos">José Eduardo dos Santos</a> meets with <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Angola's motto is <i>Virtus Unita Fortior</i>, a <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> phrase meaning "Virtue is stronger when united". The Angolan government is composed of three branches of government: executive, legislative, and judicial. The executive branch of the government is composed of the President, the Vice-Presidents and the Council of Ministers. The legislative branch contains a 220-seat <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> legislature elected from both provincial and nationwide constituencies. For decades, political power has been concentrated in the Presidency.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Angola" title="Constitution of Angola">Constitution of 2010</a> establishes the broad outlines of government structure and delineates the rights and duties of citizens. The legal system is based on Portuguese and customary law but is weak and fragmented, and courts operate in only 12 of more than 140 municipalities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A Supreme Court serves as the appellate tribunal; a Constitutional Court holds the powers of judicial review. Governors of the 18 provinces are appointed by the president.</p>
<p>After the end of the Civil War the regime came under pressure from within as well as from the international environment, to become more democratic and less authoritarian. Its reaction was to operate a number of changes without substantially changing its character.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Angola is classified as 'not free' by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World" title="Freedom in the World">Freedom in the World</a> 2014 report.<sup id="cite_ref-freedomhouse_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> The report noted that the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_legislative_election,_2012" title="Angolan legislative election, 2012">August 2012 parliamentary elections</a>, in which the ruling <a href="/wiki/Popular_Movement_for_the_Liberation_of_Angola" title="Popular Movement for the Liberation of Angola" class="mw-redirect">Popular Movement for the Liberation of Angola</a> won more than 70% of the vote, suffered from serious flaws, including outdated and inaccurate voter rolls.<sup id="cite_ref-freedomhouse_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> Voter turnout dropped from 80% in 2008 to 60%.<sup id="cite_ref-freedomhouse_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Angola scored poorly on the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Index_of_African_Governance" title="Ibrahim Index of African Governance">Ibrahim Index of African Governance</a>. It was ranked 39 out of 52 <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan African</a> countries, scoring particularly badly in the areas of Participation and Human Rights, Sustainable Economic Opportunity and Human Development. The Ibrahim Index uses a number of different variables to compile its list which reflects the state of governance in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Angola" title="Constitution of Angola">new constitution</a>, adopted in 2010, further sharpened the authoritarian character of the regime. In the future, there will be no presidential elections: the president and the vice-president of the political party which comes out strongest in the parliamentary elections become automatically president and vice-president of Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Through a variety of mechanisms, the state president controls all the other organs of the state, so that the principle of the division of power is not maintained. As a consequence, Angola has no longer a presidential system, in the sense of the systems existing e.g. in the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">USA</a> or in <a href="/wiki/French_government" title="French government" class="mw-redirect">France</a>. In terms of the classifications used in constitutional law, its regime is considered one of several authoritarian regimes in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 16 October 2014, Angola was elected for the second time as non-permanent member of the UN Security Council, with 190 favourable votes out of 193. The mandate begins on 1 January 2015 and lasts for two years.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Also in that month, the country took on the leadership of the Group of African Ministers and Governors at the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, following the debates at the annual meetings of both entities.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Since January 2014 the Republic of Angola holds the presidency of the <a href="/wiki/International_Conference_on_the_Great_Lakes_Region" title="International Conference on the Great Lakes Region">International Conference on the Great Lakes Region</a> (ICGLR).<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2015, the executive secretary of ICGLR, <a href="/wiki/Ntumba_Luaba" title="Ntumba Luaba">Ntumba Luaba</a>, said that Angola is the example to be followed by members of the organization, because of the significant progress made over the 12 years of peace, particularly in terms of socio-economic and political-military stability.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Angolan_Air_Force_Ilyushin_Il-76TD_Karpezo-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Angolan_Air_Force_Ilyushin_Il-76TD_Karpezo-1.jpg/220px-Angolan_Air_Force_Ilyushin_Il-76TD_Karpezo-1.jpg" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Angolan_Air_Force_Ilyushin_Il-76TD_Karpezo-1.jpg/330px-Angolan_Air_Force_Ilyushin_Il-76TD_Karpezo-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Angolan_Air_Force_Ilyushin_Il-76TD_Karpezo-1.jpg/440px-Angolan_Air_Force_Ilyushin_Il-76TD_Karpezo-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="722" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Angolan_Air_Force_Ilyushin_Il-76TD_Karpezo-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Angolan Air Force Ilyushin Il-76TD Karpezo-1</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Armed_Forces" title="Angolan Armed Forces">Angolan Armed Forces</a></div>
<p>The Angolan Armed Forces (AAF) is headed by a Chief of Staff who reports to the Minister of Defense. There are three divisions—the Army (Exército), Navy (Marinha de Guerra, MGA), and <a href="/wiki/National_Air_Force_of_Angola" title="National Air Force of Angola">National Air Force</a> (Força Aérea Nacional, FAN). Total manpower is about 110,000.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Its equipment includes Russian-manufactured fighters, bombers, and transport planes. There are also Brazilian-made EMB-312 Tucano for training role, Czech-made L-39 for training and bombing role, Czech Zlin for training role and a variety of western made aircraft such as C-212\Aviocar, Sud Aviation Alouette III, etc. A small number of AAF personnel are stationed in the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> (Kinshasa) and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> (Brazzaville).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Police">Police</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Police">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The National Police departments are Public Order, Criminal Investigation, Traffic and Transport, Investigation and Inspection of Economic Activities, Taxation and Frontier Supervision, Riot Police and the Rapid Intervention Police. The National Police are in the process of standing up an air wing, which will provide helicopter support for operations. The National Police are developing their criminal investigation and forensic capabilities. The force has an estimated 6,000 patrol officers, 2,500 taxation and frontier supervision officers, 182 criminal investigators and 100 financial crimes detectives and around 90 economic activity inspectors.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The National Police have implemented a modernization and development plan to increase the capabilities and efficiency of the total force. In addition to administrative reorganization, modernization projects include procurement of new vehicles, aircraft and equipment, construction of new police stations and forensic laboratories, restructured training programs and the replacement of <a href="/wiki/AKM_rifle" title="AKM rifle" class="mw-redirect">AKM rifles</a> with 9&#160;mm <a href="/wiki/Uzi" title="Uzi">Uzis</a> for officers in urban areas.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Angola_transito.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Angola_transito.jpg/220px-Angola_transito.jpg" width="220" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Angola_transito.jpg/330px-Angola_transito.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Angola_transito.jpg/440px-Angola_transito.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="478" /></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Justice">Justice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Justice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2014, it is expected to enter into effect a new Penal Code in Angola. The classification of the money laundering crime is one of the novelties in the new legislation.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Angola_Provinces_numbered_300px.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Angola_Provinces_numbered_300px.png/220px-Angola_Provinces_numbered_300px.png" width="220" height="249" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/be/Angola_Provinces_numbered_300px.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/be/Angola_Provinces_numbered_300px.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="340" /></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exclave_of_Cabinda">Exclave of Cabinda</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Exclave of Cabinda">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_(province)" title="Cabinda (province)" class="mw-redirect">Cabinda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Cabinda" title="Republic of Cabinda">Republic of Cabinda</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Cabinda.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Flag_of_Cabinda.svg/220px-Flag_of_Cabinda.svg.png" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Flag_of_Cabinda.svg/330px-Flag_of_Cabinda.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Flag_of_Cabinda.svg/440px-Flag_of_Cabinda.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Cabinda.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Flag of the <a href="/wiki/Front_for_the_Liberation_of_the_Enclave_of_Cabinda" title="Front for the Liberation of the Enclave of Cabinda">Front for the Liberation of the Enclave of Cabinda (FLEC)</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With an area of approximately 7,283 square kilometres (2,812&#160;sq&#160;mi), the Northern Angolan province of Cabinda is unusual in being separated from the rest of the country by a strip, some 60 kilometres (37&#160;mi) wide, of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of Congo" class="mw-redirect">Democratic Republic of Congo</a> along the lower <a href="/wiki/Congo_river" title="Congo river" class="mw-redirect">Congo river</a>. Cabinda borders the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Republic" title="Congo Republic" class="mw-redirect">Congo Republic</a> to the north and north-northeast and the DRC to the east and south. The town of Cabinda is the chief population center.</p>
<p>According to a 1995 census, Cabinda had an estimated population of 600,000, approximately 400,000 of whom live in neighboring countries. Population estimates are, however, highly unreliable. Consisting largely of tropical forest, Cabinda produces hardwoods, coffee, cocoa, crude rubber and palm oil. The product for which it is best known, however, is its oil, which has given it the nickname, "the Kuwait of Africa". Cabinda's petroleum production from its considerable offshore reserves now accounts for more than half of Angola's output.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> Most of the oil along its coast was discovered under <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Angola" title="Portuguese Angola">Portuguese rule</a> by the Cabinda Gulf Oil Company (CABGOC) from 1968 onwards.</p>
<p>Ever since <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> handed over sovereignty of its former overseas province of Angola to the local independence groups (MPLA, UNITA, and FNLA), the territory of Cabinda has been a focus of separatist guerrilla actions opposing the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Angola" title="Government of Angola" class="mw-redirect">Government of Angola</a> (which has employed its military forces, the FAA—Forças Armadas Angolanas) and Cabindan separatists. The <a href="/wiki/Front_for_the_Liberation_of_the_Enclave_of_Cabinda" title="Front for the Liberation of the Enclave of Cabinda">Front for the Liberation of the Enclave of Cabinda</a>-<a href="/wiki/For%C3%A7as_Armadas_de_Cabinda" title="Forças Armadas de Cabinda">Armed Forces of Cabinda</a> (FLEC-FAC) announced a virtual Federal Republic of Cabinda under the Presidency of N'Zita Henriques Tiago. One of the characteristics of the Cabindan independence movement is its constant fragmentation, into smaller and smaller factions.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Angola" title="Economy of Angola">Economy of Angola</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_3_(8222830479).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_3_%288222830479%29.jpg/220px-First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_3_%288222830479%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_3_%288222830479%29.jpg/330px-First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_3_%288222830479%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_3_%288222830479%29.jpg/440px-First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_3_%288222830479%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TAAG_777-3M2ER.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/TAAG_777-3M2ER.jpg/220px-TAAG_777-3M2ER.jpg" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/TAAG_777-3M2ER.jpg/330px-TAAG_777-3M2ER.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/TAAG_777-3M2ER.jpg/440px-TAAG_777-3M2ER.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5057" data-file-height="3069" /></a>
