<a href="/wiki/TAAG_Angolan_Airlines" title="TAAG Angolan Airlines" class="mw-redirect">TAAG Angolan Airlines</a> is Angola's national airline</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Angola's financial system is maintained by the <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_Angola" title="National Bank of Angola">National Bank of Angola</a> and managed by Governor <a href="//no.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jose_de_Lima_Massano" class="extiw" title="no:Jose de Lima Massano">Jose de Lima Massano</a>. Angola has a rich subsoil heritage, from diamonds, oil, gold, copper, and a rich wildlife (dramatically impoverished during the civil war), forest, and fossils. Since independence, oil and diamonds have been the most important economic resource. Smallholder and plantation agriculture have dramatically dropped because of the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">Angolan Civil War</a>, but have begun to recover after 2002. The transformation industry that had come into existence in the late colonial period collapsed at independence, because of the exodus of most of the ethnic Portuguese population, but has begun to reemerge (with updated technologies), partly because of the influx of new Portuguese entrepreneurs. Similar developments can be verified in the service sector.</p>
<p>Overall, Angola's economy has undergone a period of transformation in recent years, moving from the disarray caused by a quarter century of civil war to being the fastest growing economy in Africa and one of the fastest in the world, with an average GDP growth of 20 percent between 2005 and 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> In the period 2001–2010, Angola had the world's highest <a href="/wiki/Annual_average_GDP_growth" title="Annual average GDP growth" class="mw-redirect">annual average GDP growth</a>, at 11.1 percent. In 2004, China's <a href="/wiki/Eximbank" title="Eximbank" class="mw-redirect">Eximbank</a> approved a $2&#160;billion line of credit to Angola. The loan is being used to rebuild Angola's infrastructure, and has also limited the influence of the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> China is Angola's biggest trade partner and export destination as well as the fourth-largest importer. Bilateral trade reached $27.67 billion in 2011, up 11.5 percent year-on-year. China's imports, mainly crude oil and diamonds, increased 9.1 percent to $24.89 billion while China's exports, including mechanical and electrical products, machinery parts and construction materials, surged 38.8 percent.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The overabundance of oil led to a local unleaded gasoline "pricetag" of <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">£</a>0.37 per gallon.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>The Economist</i> reported in 2008 that diamonds and oil make up 60 percent of Angola's economy, almost all of the country's revenue and are its dominant exports.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> Growth is almost entirely driven by rising <a href="/wiki/Extraction_of_petroleum" title="Extraction of petroleum">oil production</a> which surpassed 1.4 million barrels per day (220,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d) in late 2005 and was expected to grow to 2 million barrels per day (320,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d) by 2007. Control of the <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry" title="Petroleum industry">oil industry</a> is consolidated in <a href="/wiki/Sonangol_Group" title="Sonangol Group">Sonangol Group</a>, a conglomerate which is owned by the Angolan government. In December 2006, Angola was admitted as a member of <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> However, operations in <a href="/wiki/List_of_diamond_mines" title="List of diamond mines">diamond mines</a> include partnerships between state-run <a href="/wiki/Endiama" title="Endiama">Endiama</a> and mining companies such as <a href="/wiki/ALROSA" title="ALROSA">ALROSA</a> which continue operations in Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> The economy grew 18% in 2005, 26% in 2006 and 17.6% in 2007. However, due to the global recession the economy contracted an estimated −0.3% in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> The security brought about by the 2002 peace settlement has led to the resettlement of 4&#160;million displaced persons, thus resulting in large-scale increases in agriculture production.</p>
<p>Although the country's economy has developed significantly since achieving political stability in 2002, mainly thanks to the fast-rising earnings of the oil sector, Angola faces huge social and economic problems. These are in part a result of the almost continual state of conflict from 1961 onwards, although the highest level of destruction and socio-economic damage took place after the 1975 independence, during the long years of <a href="/wiki/Angolan_civil_war" title="Angolan civil war" class="mw-redirect">civil war</a>. However, high poverty rates and blatant social inequality are chiefly the outcome of a combination of a persistent political authoritarianism, of "neo-patrimonial" practices at all levels of the political, administrative, military, and economic apparatuses, and of <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Angola" title="Corruption in Angola">a pervasive corruption</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> The main beneficiary of this situation is a social segment constituted since 1975, but mainly during the last decades, around the political, administrative, economic, and military power holders, which has accumulated (and continues accumulating) enormous wealth.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> "Secondary beneficiaries" are the middle strata which are about to become social classes. However, overall almost half the population has to be considered as poor, but in this respect there are dramatic differences between the countryside and the cities (where by now slightly more than 50% of the people live).</p>
<p>An inquiry carried out in 2008 by the Angolan Instituto Nacional de Estatística has it that in the rural areas roughly 58% must be classified as "poor", according to UN norms, but in the urban areas only 19%, while the overall rate is 37%.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> In the cities, a majority of families, well beyond those officially classified as poor, have to adopt a variety of survival strategies.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> At the same time, in urban areas social inequality is most evident, and assumes extreme forms in the capital, Luanda.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> Angola constantly ranks in the bottom group.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/The_Heritage_Foundation" title="The Heritage Foundation">The Heritage Foundation</a>, a conservative American <a href="/wiki/Think_tank" title="Think tank">think tank</a>, oil production from Angola has increased so significantly that Angola now is China's biggest supplier of oil.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> Growing oil revenues have also created opportunities for <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Angola" title="Corruption in Angola">corruption</a>: according to a recent <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> report, 32 billion US dollars disappeared from government accounts from 2007 to 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Before independence in 1975, <a href="/wiki/Angola_(Portugal)" title="Angola (Portugal)" class="mw-redirect">Angola</a> was a breadbasket of southern Africa and a major exporter of <a href="/wiki/Bananas" title="Bananas" class="mw-redirect">bananas</a>, coffee and <a href="/wiki/Sisal" title="Sisal">sisal</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">three decades of civil war</a> (1975–2002) destroyed the fertile countryside, leaving it littered with landmines and driving millions into the cities. The country now depends on expensive food imports, mainly from South Africa and <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, while more than 90 percent of farming is done at family and subsistence level. Thousands of Angolan small-scale farmers are trapped in poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The enormous differences between the regions pose a serious structural problem in the Angolan economy. This is best illustrated by the fact that about one third of the economic activities is concentrated in Luanda and the neighbouring Bengo province, while several areas of the interior are characterized by stagnation and even regression.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>One of the economic consequences of the social and regional disparities is a sharp increase in Angolan private investments abroad. The small fringe of Angolan society where most of the accumulation takes place seeks to spread its assets, for reasons of security and profit. For the time being, the biggest share of these investments is concentrated in Portugal where the <a href="/wiki/Angolans_in_Portugal" title="Angolans in Portugal">Angolan presence</a> (including that of the family of the state president) in <a href="/wiki/Bank" title="Bank">banks</a> as well as in the domains of energy, <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Angola" title="Telecommunications in Angola">telecommunications</a>, and mass media has become notable, as has the acquisition of vineyards and orchards as well as of touristic enterprises.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>With a stock of assets corresponding to 70 billion USD (6.8 billion Kz), Angola is now the third largest financial market in sub-Saharan Africa, surpassed only by <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>. According to the Angolan Minister of Economy, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Abra%C3%A3o_Gourgel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Abraão Gourgel (page does not exist)">Abraão Gourgel</a>, the financial market of the country grew modestly from 2002 and now lies in third place at the level of sub-Saharan Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Angola’s economy is expected to grow by 3.9 percent in 2014 said the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF). According to the Fund, robust growth in the nonoil economy, mainly driven by a very good performance in the agricultural sector, is expected to offset a temporary drop in oil production.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>According to a study on the banking sector, carried out by <a href="/wiki/Deloitte" title="Deloitte">Deloitte</a>, the monetary policy led by <a href="/wiki/Banco_Nacional_de_Angola" title="Banco Nacional de Angola" class="mw-redirect">Banco Nacional de Angola</a> (BNA), the Angolan national bank, allowed a decrease in the inflation rate put at 7.96% in December 2013, which contributed to the sector’s growth trend.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>According to estimates divulged by Angola’s central bank, the country’s economy should grow at an annual average rate of 5 percent over the next four years, boosted by the increasing participation of the private sector.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 19 December 2014, the Capital Market in Angola started. <a href="/wiki/Angola_Stock_Exchange" title="Angola Stock Exchange">BODIVA</a> (Angola Securities and Debt Stock Exchange, in English) received the secondary public debt market, and it is expected to start the corporate debt market by 2015, but the stock market should only be a reality in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Angola" title="Transport in Angola">Transport in Angola</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aeroport-4-de-Fevereiro-Chegadas_LWS1962.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Aeroport-4-de-Fevereiro-Chegadas_LWS1962.JPG/220px-Aeroport-4-de-Fevereiro-Chegadas_LWS1962.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Aeroport-4-de-Fevereiro-Chegadas_LWS1962.JPG/330px-Aeroport-4-de-Fevereiro-Chegadas_LWS1962.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Aeroport-4-de-Fevereiro-Chegadas_LWS1962.JPG/440px-Aeroport-4-de-Fevereiro-Chegadas_LWS1962.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aeroport-4-de-Fevereiro-Chegadas_LWS1962.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Luanda_Airport" title="Luanda Airport" class="mw-redirect">Quatro de Fevereiro Luanda Airport</a> arrivals</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Transport in Angola consists of:</p>
<ul>
<li>Three separate <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Angola" title="Rail transport in Angola">railway systems</a> totalling 2,761&#160;km (1,715&#160;mi)</li>
<li>76,626&#160;km (47,613&#160;mi) of highway of which 19,156&#160;km (11,903&#160;mi) is paved</li>
<li>1,295 navigable inland waterways</li>
<li>Eight major <a href="/wiki/Sea_port" title="Sea port" class="mw-redirect">sea ports</a></li>
<li>243 <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Angola" title="List of airports in Angola">airports</a>, of which 32 are paved.</li>
</ul>
<p>Travel on highways outside of towns and cities in Angola (and in some cases within) is often not best advised for those without four-by-four vehicles. While a reasonable road infrastructure has existed within Angola, time and the war have taken their toll on the road surfaces, leaving many severely potholed, littered with broken asphalt. In many areas drivers have established alternate tracks to avoid the worst parts of the surface, although careful attention must be paid to the presence or absence of landmine warning markers by the side of the road. The Angolan government has contracted the restoration of many of the country's roads. The road between Lubango and Namibe, for example, was completed recently with funding from the European Union, and is comparable to many European main routes. Progress to complete the road infrastructure is likely to take some decades, but substantial efforts are already being made in the right directions.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications">Telecommunications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Telecommunications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications" title="Telecommunications" class="mw-redirect">telecommunications</a> industry is considered one of the main strategic sectors in Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/October" title="October">October</a> <a href="/wiki/2014" title="2014">2014</a>, the building of the first <a href="/wiki/Optic_fiber" title="Optic fiber" class="mw-redirect">optic fiber</a> underwater cable in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a> was announced.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> This project aims to turn Angola into a continental hub, thus improving <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> connections both nationally and internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 11 <a href="/wiki/March" title="March">March</a> <a href="/wiki/2015" title="2015">2015</a>, the First Angolan Forum of Telecommunications and Information Technology was held, in <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a> under the motto "The challenges of telecommunications in the current context of Angola".<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> The purpose of this forum was to promote the debate on topical issues on <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications" title="Telecommunications" class="mw-redirect">telecommunications</a> in Angola and worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The first Angolan <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellite</a>, AngoSat-1, will be ready for launch into <a href="/wiki/Orbit" title="Orbit">orbit</a> in <a href="/wiki/2016" title="2016">2016</a> and will ensure telecommunications throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Aristides Safeca, Secretary of State for Telecommunications, the satellite will provide <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications" title="Telecommunications" class="mw-redirect">telecommunications</a> services, <a href="/wiki/TV" title="TV" class="mw-redirect">TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">internet</a> and <a href="/wiki/E-government" title="E-government" class="mw-redirect">e-government</a> and will remain into orbit "at best" for 18 years.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The management of the domain '.ao' on web pages, will go from <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> to Angola in 2015, following the approval of a new legislation by the Angolan Government.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> The joint decree of the minister of Telecommunications and Information Technologies, José Carvalho da Rocha, and the minister of Science and Technology, Maria Cândida Pereira Teixeira, states that "under the massification" of that Angolan domain, "conditions are created for the transfer of the domain root '.ao' of Portugal to Angola”.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Angola" title="Demographics of Angola">Demographics of Angola</a></div>
<p>Angola has a population of 24,383,301 inhabitants according to the preliminary results of its 2014 census, the first one conducted or carried out since 15 December 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-unpop_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unpop-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> It is composed of <a href="/wiki/Ovimbundu" title="Ovimbundu">Ovimbundu</a> (language <a href="/wiki/Umbundu" title="Umbundu">Umbundu</a>) 37%, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mbundu_people" title="Northern Mbundu people" class="mw-redirect">Ambundu</a> (language <a href="/wiki/Kimbundu" title="Kimbundu">Kimbundu</a>) 25%, <a href="/wiki/Bakongo" title="Bakongo" class="mw-redirect">Bakongo</a> 13%, and 32% other ethnic groups (including the <a href="/wiki/Chokwe_people" title="Chokwe people">Chokwe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ovambo_people" title="Ovambo people">Ovambo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mbunda" title="Mbunda" class="mw-redirect">Mbunda</a>, with the latter having been replaced by <a href="/wiki/Ganguela" title="Ganguela">Ganguela</a>, a generic term for peoples east of the Central Highlands,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> which has a slightly derogatory meaning when applied by the western ethnic groups,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Xindonga" title="Xindonga">Xindonga</a>) as well as about 2% <i>mestiços</i> (mixed European and African), 1.4% Chinese and 1% European.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> The Ambundu and Ovimbundu nations combined form a majority of the population, at 62%.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> The population is forecast to grow to over 60 million people to 2050, 2.7 times the 2014 population.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>It is estimated that Angola was host to 12,100 refugees and 2,900 asylum seekers by the end of 2007. 11,400 of those refugees were originally from the Democratic Republic of Congo, who arrived in the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2008 there were an estimated 400,000 <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> migrant workers,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> at least 30,000 <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Angolans" title="Portuguese Angolans">Portuguese</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> and about 259,000 <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people_in_Angola" title="Chinese people in Angola">Chinese living in Angola</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Since 2003, more than 400,000 <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congolese</a> migrants have been expelled from Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> Prior to independence in 1975, Angola had a community of approximately 350,000 Portuguese,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> but the vast majority left after independence and the ensuing civil war. However, Angola has recovered its Portuguese minority in recent years; currently, there are about 200,000 registered with the consulates, and increasing due to the debt crisis in Portugal and the relative prosperity in Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> The Chinese population stands at 258,920, mostly composed of temporary migrants.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> of Angola is 5.54 children born per woman (2012 estimates), the 11th highest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Angola" title="Languages of Angola">Languages of Angola</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CPLP_map-pt.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/CPLP_map-pt.svg/220px-CPLP_map-pt.svg.png" width="220" height="97" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/CPLP_map-pt.svg/330px-CPLP_map-pt.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/CPLP_map-pt.svg/440px-CPLP_map-pt.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="940" data-file-height="415" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CPLP_map-pt.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Angola is a member of <a href="/wiki/CPLP" title="CPLP" class="mw-redirect">CPLP</a> – Community of Portuguese speaking nations</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The languages in Angola are those originally spoken by the different ethnic groups and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, introduced during the Portuguese colonial era. The indigenous languages with the largest usage are <a href="/wiki/Umbundu" title="Umbundu">Umbundu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kimbundu" title="Kimbundu">Kimbundu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kikongo" title="Kikongo" class="mw-redirect">Kikongo</a>, in that order. Portuguese is the official language of the country.</p>
<p>Mastery of the official language is probably more extended in Angola than it is elsewhere in Africa, and this certainly applies to its use in everyday life. Moreover, and above all, the proportion of native (or near native) speakers of the language of the former colonizer, turned official after independence, is no doubt considerably higher than in any other African country.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>There are three intertwined historical reasons for this situation.</p>
<ol>
<li>In the Portuguese "bridgeheads" <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Benguela" title="Benguela">Benguela</a>, which existed on the coast of what today is Angola since the 15th and 16th century, respectively, Portuguese was spoken not only by the Portuguese and their <i>mestiço</i> descendents, but—especially in and around Luanda—by a significant number of Africans, although these always remained native speakers of their local African language.</li>
<li>Since the Portuguese conquest of the present territory of Angola, and especially since its "effective occupation" in the mid-1920s, schooling in Portuguese was slowly developed by the colonial state as well as by Catholic and Protestant missions. The rhythm of this expansion was considerably accelerated during the late colonial period, 1961–1974, so that by the end of the colonial period children all over the territory (with relatively few exceptions) had at least some access to the Portuguese language.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In the same late colonial period, the legal discrimination of the black population was abolished, and the state apparatus in fields like health, education, social work, and rural development was enlarged. This entailed a significant increase in jobs for Africans, under the condition that they spoke Portuguese.</li>
</ol>
<p>As a consequence of all this, the African “lower middle class” which at that stage formed in Luanda and other cities began to often prevent their children from learning the local African language, in order to guarantee that they learned Portuguese as their native language. At the same time, the white and “mestiço” population, where some knowledge of African languages could previously often been found, neglected this aspect more and more, to the point of frequently ignoring it totally. After independence, these tendencies continued, and were even strengthened, under the rule of the MPLA which has its main social roots exactly in those social segments where the mastery of Portuguese as well as the proportion of native Portuguese speakers was highest. This became a political side issue, as FNLA and UNITA, given their regional constituencies, came out in favour of a greater attention to the African languages, and as the FNLA favoured French over Portuguese.</p>
<p>The dynamics of the language situation, as described above, were additionally fostered by the massive migrations triggered by the Civil War. <a href="/wiki/Ovimbundu" title="Ovimbundu">Ovimbundu</a>, the most populous ethnic group and the most affected by the war, appeared in great numbers in urban areas outside their areas, especially in Luanda and surroundings. At the same time, a majority of the <a href="/wiki/Bakongo" title="Bakongo" class="mw-redirect">Bakongo</a> who had fled to the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of Congo" class="mw-redirect">Democratic Republic of Congo</a> in the early 1960s, or of their children and grandchildren, returned to Angola, but mostly did not settle in their original "habitat", but in the cities—and again above all in Luanda. As a consequence, more than half the population is now living in the cities which, from the linguistic point of view, have become highly heterogeneous. This means, of course, that Portuguese as the overall national language of communication is by now of paramount importance, and that the role of the African languages is steadily decreasing among the urban population—a trend which is beginning to spread into rural areas as well.</p>
<p>The exact numbers of those fluent in Portuguese or who speak Portuguese as a first language are unknown, although a census is expected to be carried out in July–August 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Precise_language" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="According to the source, the census will have started as of 16 July 2013.">dated info</span></a></i>]</sup> Quite a number of voices demand the recognition of "Angolan Portuguese" as a specific variant, comparable to those spoken in Portugal or in Brazil. However, while there exists a certain number of idiomatic particularities in everyday Portuguese, as spoken by Angolans, it remains to be seen whether or not the Angolan government comes to the conclusion that these particularities constitute a configuration that justifies the claim to be a new language variant.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Angola" title="Religion in Angola">Religion in Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Angola" title="Christianity in Angola">Christianity in Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Angola" title="Islam in Angola">Islam in Angola</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Angola_Ethnic_map_1970.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Angola_Ethnic_map_1970.svg/220px-Angola_Ethnic_map_1970.svg.png" width="220" height="282" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Angola_Ethnic_map_1970.svg/330px-Angola_Ethnic_map_1970.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Angola_Ethnic_map_1970.svg/440px-Angola_Ethnic_map_1970.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="820" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Angola_Ethnic_map_1970.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ethnic groups of Angola 1970 (with areas where the so-called "Ganguela" groups are dominant, marked green)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are about 1000 mostly Christian religious communities in Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> While reliable statistics are nonexistent, estimates have it that more than half of the population are Catholics, while about a quarter adhere to the Protestant churches introduced during the colonial period: the <a href="/wiki/Congregationalist" title="Congregationalist" class="mw-redirect">Congregationalists</a> mainly among the <a href="/wiki/Ovimbundu" title="Ovimbundu">Ovimbundu</a> of the Central Highlands and the coastal region to its West, the <a href="/wiki/Methodists" title="Methodists" class="mw-redirect">Methodists</a> concentrating on the <a href="/wiki/Kimbundu" title="Kimbundu">Kimbundu</a> speaking strip from Luanda to Malanje, the <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a> almost exclusively among the <a href="/wiki/Bakongo" title="Bakongo" class="mw-redirect">Bakongo</a> of the Northwest (now massively present in Luanda as well) and dispersed <a href="/wiki/Adventists" title="Adventists" class="mw-redirect">Adventists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reformed" title="Reformed" class="mw-redirect">Reformed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lutherans" title="Lutherans" class="mw-redirect">Lutherans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> In Luanda and region there subsists a nucleus of the "<a href="/wiki/Syncretic" title="Syncretic" class="mw-redirect">syncretic</a>" <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tocoists&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tocoists (page does not exist)">Tocoists</a> and in the northwest a sprinkling of <a href="/wiki/Kimbanguism" title="Kimbanguism">Kimbanguism</a> can be found, spreading from the Congo/Zaire. Since independence, hundreds of <a href="/wiki/Pentecostal" title="Pentecostal" class="mw-redirect">Pentecostal</a> and similar communities have sprung up in the cities, where by now about 50% of the population is living; several of these communities/churches are of Brazilian origin.</p>
<p>The U.S. Department of State estimates the Muslim population at 80,000–90,000,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> while the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Islamic_Community_of_Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Islamic Community of Angola (page does not exist)">Islamic Community of Angola</a> puts the figure closer to 500,000.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> Muslims consist largely of migrants from West Africa and the Middle East (especially <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>), although some are local converts.<sup id="cite_ref-customs_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-customs-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> The Angolan government does not <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Angola#Legal_status" title="Islam in Angola">legally recognize</a> any Muslim organizations and often shuts down mosques or prevents their construction.<sup id="cite_ref-IRFR2012_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR2012-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In a study assessing nations' levels of religious regulation and persecution with scores ranging from 0 to 10 where 0 represented low levels of regulation or persecution, Angola was scored 0.8 on Government Regulation of Religion, 4.0 on Social Regulation of Religion, 0 on Government Favoritism of Religion and 0 on Religious Persecution.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Foreign <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionaries</a> were very active prior to independence in 1975, although since the beginning of the anti-colonial fight in 1961 the Portuguese colonial authorities expelled a series of Protestant missionaries and closed mission stations based on the belief that the missionaries were inciting pro-independence sentiments. Missionaries have been able to return to the country since the early 1990s, although security conditions due to the civil war have prevented them until 2002 from restoring many of their former inland mission stations.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Catholic Church and some major Protestant denominations mostly keep to themselves in contrast to the "New Churches" which actively proselytize. Catholics, as well as some major Protestant denominations, provide help for the poor in the form of crop seeds, farm animals, medical care and education.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:African_Art,_Yombe_sculpture,_Louvre.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg/220px-African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg" width="220" height="308" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg/330px-African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg/440px-African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2670" data-file-height="3738" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:African_Art,_Yombe_sculpture,_Louvre.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Yombe_people" title="Yombe people">Yombe</a>-sculpture, 19th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Angola" title="Culture of Angola">Culture of Angola</a></div>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Angola" title="Music of Angola">Music of Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Angolan_cuisine" title="Angolan cuisine">Angolan cuisine</a></div>
<p>In Angola, there is a Culture Ministry that is managed by Culture Minister Rosa Maria Martins da Cruz e Silva.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> has been present in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_West_Africa" title="Portuguese West Africa" class="mw-redirect">Angola for 400&#160;years</a>, occupied the territory in the 19th and early 20th century, and ruled over it for about 50 years. As a consequence, both countries share cultural aspects: language (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Language" title="Portuguese Language" class="mw-redirect">Portuguese</a>) and main religion (Roman Catholic Christianity). The <i><a href="/wiki/Substratum" title="Substratum" class="mw-redirect">substrate</a></i> of Angolan culture is African, mostly <a href="/wiki/Bantu_people" title="Bantu people" class="mw-redirect">Bantu</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Portugal" title="Culture of Portugal">Portuguese culture</a> has been imported. The diverse ethnic communities – the <a href="/wiki/Ovimbundu" title="Ovimbundu">Ovimbundu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mbundu_people" title="Northern Mbundu people" class="mw-redirect">Ambundu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bakongo" title="Bakongo" class="mw-redirect">Bakongo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chokwe_people" title="Chokwe people">Chokwe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mbunda_people" title="Mbunda people">Mbunda</a> and other peoples – maintain to varying degrees their own cultural traits, traditions and languages, but in the cities, where slightly more than half of the population now lives, a mixed culture has been emerging since colonial times – in <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a> since its foundation in the 16th century. In this urban culture, the Portuguese heritage has become more and more dominant. An African influence is evident in music and dance, and is moulding the way in which Portuguese is spoken, but is almost disappearing from the vocabulary. This process is well reflected in contemporary Angolan literature, especially in the works of <a href="/wiki/Pepetela" title="Pepetela">Pepetela</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ana_Paula_Ribeiro_Tavares" title="Ana Paula Ribeiro Tavares">Ana Paula Ribeiro Tavares</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Leila_Lopes_(model)" title="Leila Lopes (model)" class="mw-redirect">Leila Lopes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miss_Angola" title="Miss Angola">Miss Angola</a> 2011, was crowned <a href="/wiki/Miss_Universe_2011" title="Miss Universe 2011">Miss Universe 2011</a> in Brazil on 12 September 2011 making her the first Angolan to win the pageant.</p>
<p>In 2014, Angola resume the National Festival of Angolan Culture (FENACULT), after a 25-years break. The festival took place in all the provincial capitals of the country between 30 August and 20 September and had as theme "Culture as a Factor of Peace and Development".<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Angolan_woman_with_children_outside_health_clinic_(5686703351).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Angolan_woman_with_children_outside_health_clinic_%285686703351%29.jpg/220px-Angolan_woman_with_children_outside_health_clinic_%285686703351%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Angolan_woman_with_children_outside_health_clinic_%285686703351%29.jpg/330px-Angolan_woman_with_children_outside_health_clinic_%285686703351%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Angolan_woman_with_children_outside_health_clinic_%285686703351%29.jpg/440px-Angolan_woman_with_children_outside_health_clinic_%285686703351%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Angolan_woman_with_children_outside_health_clinic_(5686703351).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Angolan woman with children outside health clinic</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Angola" title="Health in Angola">Health in Angola</a></div>
<p>Epidemics of <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rabies" title="Rabies">rabies</a> and African <a href="/wiki/Hemorrhagic" title="Hemorrhagic" class="mw-redirect">hemorrhagic</a> fevers like <a href="/wiki/Marburg_virus" title="Marburg virus">Marburg hemorrhagic fever</a>, are common diseases in several parts of the country. Many regions in this country have high incidence rates of <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> and high HIV prevalence rates. <a href="/wiki/Dengue" title="Dengue" class="mw-redirect">Dengue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filariasis" title="Filariasis">filariasis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leishmaniasis" title="Leishmaniasis">leishmaniasis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Onchocerciasis" title="Onchocerciasis">onchocerciasis</a> (river blindness) are other diseases carried by insects that also occur in the region. Angola has one of the highest <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality_rate" title="Infant mortality rate" class="mw-redirect">infant mortality rates</a> in the world and one of the world's lowest <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancies" title="Life expectancies" class="mw-redirect">life expectancies</a>. A 2007 survey concluded that low and deficient <a href="/wiki/Niacin" title="Niacin">niacin</a> status was common in Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Surveys" title="Demographic and Health Surveys">Demographic and Health Surveys</a> is currently conducting several surveys in Angola on malaria, domestic violence and more.<sup id="cite_ref-Angola_Surveys_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Angola_Surveys-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2014, the Angolan Institute for Cancer Control (IACC) was created by presidential decree, and it will integrate the National Health Service in Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> The purpose of this new center is to ensure the health and medical care in <a href="/wiki/Oncology" title="Oncology">oncology</a>, policy implementation, programs and plans for prevention and specialized treatment.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> This cancer institute will be assumed as a reference institution in the central and southern regions of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, Angola launched a national campaign of vaccination against <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a>, extended to every child under ten years old and aiming to go to all 18 provinces in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> The measure is part of the Strategic Plan for the Elimination of Measles 2014–2020 created by the Angolan Ministry of Health which includes strengthening routine immunization, a proper dealing with measles cases, national campaigns, introducing a second dose of vaccination in the national routine vaccination calendar and active epidemiological surveillance for measles. This campaign took place together with the vaccination against <a href="/wiki/Polio" title="Polio" class="mw-redirect">polio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_A" title="Vitamin A">vitamin A</a> supplementation.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda,_Angola.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda%2C_Angola.jpg/220px-Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda%2C_Angola.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda%2C_Angola.jpg/330px-Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda%2C_Angola.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda%2C_Angola.jpg/440px-Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda%2C_Angola.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda,_Angola.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lyceum Salvador Correia in Luanda</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuito_class.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Kuito_class.jpg/220px-Kuito_class.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Kuito_class.jpg/330px-Kuito_class.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Kuito_class.jpg/440px-Kuito_class.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuito_class.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Kuito class, Angola</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Angola" title="Education in Angola">Education in Angola</a></div>
<p>Although by law education in Angola is compulsory and free for eight years, the government reports that a percentage of students are not attending due to a lack of school buildings and teachers.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Students are often responsible for paying additional school-related expenses, including fees for books and supplies.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1999, the gross primary enrollment rate was 74 percent and in 1998, the most recent year for which data are available, the net primary enrollment rate was 61 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_108-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Gross and net enrollment ratios are based on the number of students formally registered in primary school and therefore do not necessarily reflect actual school attendance.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_108-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> There continue to be significant disparities in enrollment between rural and urban areas. In 1995, 71.2 percent of children ages 7 to 14 years were attending school.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_108-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> It is reported that higher percentages of boys attend school than girls.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_108-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">Angolan Civil War</a> (1975–2002), nearly half of all schools were reportedly looted and destroyed, leading to current problems with overcrowding.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_108-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Ministry of Education hired 20,000 new teachers in 2005 and continued to implement teacher trainings.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_108-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Teachers tend to be underpaid, inadequately trained, and overworked (sometimes teaching two or three shifts a day).<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_108-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Some teachers may reportedly demand payment or bribes directly from their students.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_108-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Other factors, such as the presence of landmines, lack of resources and identity papers, and poor health prevent children from regularly attending school.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_108-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Although budgetary allocations for education were increased in 2004, the education system in Angola continues to be extremely under-funded.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_108-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>According to estimates by the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Institute_for_Statistics" title="UNESCO Institute for Statistics">UNESCO Institute for Statistics</a>, the adult literacy rate in 2011 was 70.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-unescolit_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unescolit-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> 82.9% of males and 54.2% of women are literate as of 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> Since independence from Portugal in 1975, a number of Angolan students continued to be admitted every year at high schools, <a href="/wiki/Polytechnical" title="Polytechnical" class="mw-redirect">polytechnical</a> institutes, and universities in <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, Brazil and <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> through bilateral agreements; in general, these students belong to the elites.</p>
<p>In September 2014, the Angolan Ministry of Education announced an investment of 16 million Euros in the computerization of over 300 classrooms across the country. The project also includes training teachers at a national level, “as a way to introduce and use new information technologies in primary schools, thus reflecting an improvement in the quality of teaching.”<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, the Angolan Government started building the Angolan Media Libraries Network, a set of infrastructures distributed throughout several provinces in the country to facilitate the people’s access to information and knowledge. Each site has a bibliographic archive, multimedia resources and computers with Internet access, as well as areas for reading, researching and socializing.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> The plan envisages the establishment of one media library in each Angolan province by 2017. The project also includes the implementation of several media libraries, in order to provide the several contents available in the fixed media libraries to the most isolated populations in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> At this time, the mobile media libraries are already operating in the provinces of Luanda, Malanje, Uíge, Cabinda and Lunda South. As for REMA, the provinces of Luanda, Benguela, Lubango and Soyo have currently working media libraries.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Angola is the top basketball team of <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Africa" title="FIBA Africa">FIBA Africa</a>, and a regular competitor at the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_Summer_Olympics" title="Basketball at the Summer Olympics">Summer Olympic Games</a> and the <a href="/wiki/FIBA_World_Cup" title="FIBA World Cup" class="mw-redirect">FIBA World Cup</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Angola_national_football_team" title="Angola national football team">Angola national football team</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a>, as this was their first appearance on the World Cup finals stage. They were eliminated after one defeat and two draws in the group stage. They won 3 <a href="/wiki/COSAFA_Cup" title="COSAFA Cup">COSAFA Cups</a> and finished runner up in <a href="/wiki/2011_African_Nations_Championship" title="2011 African Nations Championship">2011 African Nations Championship</a>. Angola has participated in the <a href="/wiki/World_Women%27s_Handball_Championship" title="World Women's Handball Championship" class="mw-redirect">World Women's Handball Championship</a> for several years. The country has also appeared in the <a href="/wiki/Angola_at_the_Olympics" title="Angola at the Olympics">Summer Olympics</a> for seven years and both compete and have hosted the <a href="/wiki/FIRS_Roller_Hockey_World_Cup" title="FIRS Roller Hockey World Cup">FIRS Roller Hockey World Cup</a>. Angola is also often believed to have historic roots in the <a href="/wiki/Martial_art" title="Martial art" class="mw-redirect">martial art</a> "<a href="/wiki/Capoeira_Angola" title="Capoeira Angola" class="mw-redirect">Capoeira Angola</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Batuque_(game)" title="Batuque (game)">Batuque</a>" which were practiced by <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Angola" title="Slavery in Angola">enslaved African Angolans</a> transported as part of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

As he had obtained a relative, but not absolute majority of votes in the 1992 presidential election, a second round—opposing him to <a href="/wiki/Jonas_Savimbi" title="Jonas Savimbi">Jonas Savimbi</a>—was constitutionally necessary to make his election effective, but he preferred never to hold this second round.</span></li>
